[Support](#support)\\\\n\\\\n## API Credentials & Required Scopes\\\\n\\\\n### Setting Up CrowdStrike API Credentials\\\\n\\\\nBefore using the Falcon MCP Server, you need to create API credentials in your CrowdStrike console:\\\\n\\\\n1. **Log into your CrowdStrike console**\\\\n2. **Navigate to Support > API Clients and Keys**\\\\n3. **Click \\\\"Add new API client\\\\"**\\\\n4. **Configure your API client**:\\\\n   * **Client Name**: Choose a descriptive name (e.g., \\\\"Falcon MCP Server\\\\")\\\\n   * **Description**: Optional description for your records\\\\n   * **API Scopes**: Select the scopes based on which modules you plan to use (see below)\\\\n\\\\n> **Important**: Ensure your API client has the necessary scopes for the modules you plan to use. You can always update scopes later in the CrowdStrike console.\\\\n\\\\n### Required API Scopes by Module\\\\n\\\\nThe Falcon MCP Server supports different modules, each requiring specific API scopes:\\\\n\\\\n| Module | Required API Scopes | Purpose |\\\\n| --- | --- | --- |\\\\n| **Cloud Security** | `Falcon Container Image:read` | Find and analyze kubernetes containers inventory and container imges vulnerabilities |\\\\n| **Core** | *No additional scopes* | Basic connectivity and system information |\\\\n| **Detections** | `Alerts:read` | Find and analyze detections to understand malicious activity |\\\\n| **Discover** | `Assets:read` | Search and analyze application inventory across your environment |\\\\n| **Hosts** | `Hosts:read` | Manage and query host/device information |\\\\n| **Identity Protection** | `Identity Protection Entities:read` `Identity Protection Timeline:read` `Identity Protection Detections:read` `Identity Protection Assessment:read` `Identity Protection GraphQL:write` | Comprehensive entity investigation and identity protection analysis |\\\\n| **Incidents** | `Incidents:read` | Analyze security incidents and coordinated activities |\\\\n| **NGSIEM** | `NGSIEM:read` `NGSIEM:write` | Execute CQL queries against Next-Gen SIEM |\\\\n| **Intel** | `Actors (Falcon Intelligence):read` `Indicators (Falcon Intelligence):read` `Reports (Falcon Intelligence):read` | Research threat actors, IOCs, and intelligence reports |\\\\n| **IOC** | `IOC Management:read` `IOC Management:write` | Search, create, and remove custom IOCs using IOC Service Collection endpoints |\\\\n| **Scheduled Reports** | `Scheduled Reports:read` | Get details about scheduled reports and searches, run reports on demand, and download report files |\\\\n| **Sensor Usage** | `Sensor Usage:read` | Access and analyze sensor usage data |\\\\n| **Serverless** | `Falcon Container Image:read` | Search for vulnerabilities in serverless functions across cloud service providers |\\\\n| **Spotlight** | `Vulnerabilities:read` | Manage and analyze vulnerability data and security assessments |\\\\n\\\\n## Available Modules, Tools & Resources\\\\n\\\\nImportant\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u26a0\\\\ufe0f **Important Note on FQL Guide Resources**: Several modules include FQL (Falcon Query Language) guide resources that provide comprehensive query documentation and examples. While these resources are designed to assist AI assistants and users with query construction, **FQL has nuanced syntax requirements and field-specific behaviors** that may not be immediately apparent. AI-generated FQL filters should be **tested and validated** before use in production environments. We recommend starting with simple queries and gradually building complexity while verifying results in a test environment first.\\\\n\\\\n**About Tools & Resources**: This server provides both tools (actions you can perform) and resources (documentation and context). Tools execute operations like searching for detections or analyzing threats, while resources provide comprehensive documentation like FQL query guides that AI assistants can reference for context without requiring tool calls.\\\\n\\\\n### Cloud Security Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**:\\\\n\\\\n* `Falcon Container Image:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and analyzing CrowdStrike Cloud Security resources:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_kubernetes_containers`: Search for containers from CrowdStrike Kubernetes & Containers inventory\\\\n* `falcon_count_kubernetes_containers`: Count for containers by filter criteria from CrowdStrike Kubernetes & Containers inventory\\\\n* `falcon_search_images_vulnerabilities`: Search for images vulnerabilities from CrowdStrike Image Assessments\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://cloud/kubernetes-containers/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for kubernetes containers searches\\\\n* `falcon://cloud/images-vulnerabilities/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for images vulnerabilities searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Manage kubernetes containers inventory, container images vulnerabilities analysis\\\\n\\\\n### Core Functionality (Built into Server)\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes**: *None required beyond basic API access*\\\\n\\\\nThe server provides core tools for interacting with the Falcon API:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_check_connectivity`: Check connectivity to the Falcon API\\\\n* `falcon_list_enabled_modules`: Lists enabled modules in the falcon-mcp server\\\\n  > These modules are determined by the `--modules` [flag](#module-configuration) when starting the server. If no modules are specified, all available modules are enabled.\\\\n* `falcon_list_modules`: Lists all available modules in the falcon-mcp server\\\\n\\\\n### Detections Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Alerts:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and analyzing CrowdStrike Falcon detections:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_detections`: Find and analyze detections to understand malicious activity in your environment\\\\n* `falcon_get_detection_details`: Get comprehensive detection details for specific detection IDs to understand security threats\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://detections/search/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for detection searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Threat hunting, security analysis, incident response, malware investigation\\\\n\\\\n### Discover Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Assets:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Falcon Discover applications and unmanaged assets:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_applications`: Search for applications in your CrowdStrike environment\\\\n* `falcon_search_unmanaged_assets`: Search for unmanaged assets (systems without Falcon sensor installed) that have been discovered by managed systems\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://discover/applications/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for application searches\\\\n* `falcon://discover/hosts/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for unmanaged assets searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Application inventory management, software asset management, license compliance, vulnerability assessment, unmanaged asset discovery, security gap analysis\\\\n\\\\n### Hosts Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Hosts:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Falcon hosts/devices:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_hosts`: Search for hosts in your CrowdStrike environment\\\\n* `falcon_get_host_details`: Retrieve detailed information for specified host device IDs\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://hosts/search/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for host searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Asset management, device inventory, host monitoring, compliance reporting\\\\n\\\\n### Identity Protection Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Identity Protection Entities:read`, `Identity Protection Timeline:read`, `Identity Protection Detections:read`, `Identity Protection Assessment:read`, `Identity Protection GraphQL:write`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Falcon Identity Protection capabilities:\\\\n\\\\n* `idp_investigate_entity`: Entity investigation tool for analyzing users, endpoints, and other entities with support for timeline analysis, relationship mapping, and risk assessment\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Entity investigation, identity protection analysis, user behavior analysis, endpoint security assessment, relationship mapping, risk assessment\\\\n\\\\n### Incidents Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Incidents:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and analyzing CrowdStrike Falcon incidents:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_show_crowd_score`: View calculated CrowdScores and security posture metrics for your environment\\\\n* `falcon_search_incidents`: Find and analyze security incidents to understand coordinated activity in your environment\\\\n* `falcon_get_incident_details`: Get comprehensive incident details to understand attack patterns and coordinated activities\\\\n* `falcon_search_behaviors`: Find and analyze behaviors to understand suspicious activity in your environment\\\\n* `falcon_get_behavior_details`: Get detailed behavior information to understand attack techniques and tactics\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://incidents/crowd-score/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation for CrowdScore queries\\\\n* `falcon://incidents/search/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for incident searches\\\\n* `falcon://incidents/behaviors/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for behavior searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Incident management, threat assessment, attack pattern analysis, security posture monitoring\\\\n\\\\n### NGSIEM Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `NGSIEM:read`, `NGSIEM:write`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for executing CQL queries against CrowdStrike\\\'s Next-Gen SIEM:\\\\n\\\\n* `search_ngsiem`: Execute a CQL query against Next-Gen SIEM repositories\\\\n\\\\nImportant\\\\n\\\\nThis tool executes pre-written CQL queries only. It does **not** assist with query construction or provide CQL syntax guidance. Users must supply complete, valid CQL queries. For CQL documentation, refer to the [CrowdStrike LogScale documentation](https://library.humio.com/).\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Log search and analysis, event correlation, threat hunting with custom CQL queries, security monitoring\\\\n\\\\n### Intel Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**:\\\\n\\\\n* `Actors (Falcon Intelligence):read`\\\\n* `Indicators (Falcon Intelligence):read`\\\\n* `Reports (Falcon Intelligence):read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and analyzing CrowdStrike Intelligence:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_actors`: Research threat actors and adversary groups tracked by CrowdStrike intelligence\\\\n* `falcon_search_indicators`: Search for threat indicators and indicators of compromise (IOCs) from CrowdStrike intelligence\\\\n* `falcon_search_reports`: Access CrowdStrike intelligence publications and threat reports\\\\n* `falcon_get_mitre_report`: Generate MITRE ATT&CK reports for threat actors, providing detailed tactics, techniques, and procedures (TTPs) in JSON or CSV format\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://intel/actors/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for threat actor searches\\\\n* `falcon://intel/indicators/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for indicator searches\\\\n* `falcon://intel/reports/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for intelligence report searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Threat intelligence research, adversary tracking, IOC analysis, threat landscape assessment, MITRE ATT&CK framework analysis\\\\n\\\\n### IOC Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**:\\\\n\\\\n* `IOC Management:read`\\\\n* `IOC Management:write`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for managing custom indicators of compromise (IOCs) with Falcon IOC Service Collection endpoints:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_iocs`: Search custom IOCs using FQL and return full IOC details\\\\n* `falcon_add_ioc`: Create one IOC or submit multiple IOCs in a single request\\\\n* `falcon_remove_iocs`: Remove IOCs by explicit IDs or by FQL filter for bulk cleanup\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://ioc/search/fql-guide`: FQL documentation and examples for IOC searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: IOC lifecycle management, automated IOC onboarding, IOC cleanup and hygiene workflows\\\\n\\\\n### Sensor Usage Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Sensor Usage:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and analyzing CrowdStrike Falcon sensor usage data:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_sensor_usage`: Search for weekly sensor usage data in your CrowdStrike environment\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://sensor-usage/weekly/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for sensor usage searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Sensor deployment monitoring, license utilization analysis, sensor health tracking\\\\n\\\\n### Scheduled Reports Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Scheduled Reports:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Falcon scheduled reports and scheduled searches:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_scheduled_reports`: Search for scheduled reports and searches in your CrowdStrike environment\\\\n* `falcon_launch_scheduled_report`: Launch a scheduled report on demand outside of its recurring schedule\\\\n* `falcon_search_report_executions`: Search for report executions to track status and results\\\\n* `falcon_download_report_execution`: Download generated report files\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://scheduled-reports/search/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation for searching scheduled report entities\\\\n* `falcon://scheduled-reports/executions/search/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation for searching report executions\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Automated report management, report execution monitoring, scheduled search analysis, report download automation\\\\n\\\\n### Serverless Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Falcon Container Image:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Falcon Serverless Vulnerabilities:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_serverless_vulnerabilities`: Search for vulnerabilities in your serverless functions across all cloud service providers\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://serverless/vulnerabilities/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for serverless vulnerabilities searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Serverless security assessment, vulnerability management, cloud security monitoring\\\\n\\\\n### Spotlight Module\\\\n\\\\n**API Scopes Required**: `Vulnerabilities:read`\\\\n\\\\nProvides tools for accessing and managing CrowdStrike Spotlight vulnerabilities:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon_search_vulnerabilities`: Search for vulnerabilities in your CrowdStrike environment\\\\n\\\\n**Resources**:\\\\n\\\\n* `falcon://spotlight/vulnerabilities/fql-guide`: Comprehensive FQL documentation and examples for vulnerability searches\\\\n\\\\n**Use Cases**: Vulnerability management, security assessments, compliance reporting, risk analysis, patch prioritization\\\\n\\\\n## Installation & Setup\\\\n\\\\n### Prerequisites\\\\n\\\\n* Python 3.11 or higher\\\\n* [`uv`](https://docs.astral.sh/uv/) or pip\\\\n* CrowdStrike Falcon API credentials (see above)\\\\n\\\\n### Environment Configuration\\\\n\\\\nYou can configure your CrowdStrike API credentials in several ways:\\\\n\\\\n#### Use a `.env` File\\\\n\\\\nIf you prefer using a `.env` file, you have several options:\\\\n\\\\n##### Option 1: Copy from cloned repository (if you\\\'ve cloned it)\\\\n\\\\ncp .env.example .env\\\\n\\\\n##### Option 2: Download the example file from GitHub\\\\n\\\\ncurl -o .env https://raw.githubusercontent.com/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/main/.env.example\\\\n\\\\n##### Option 3: Create manually with the following content\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Required Configuration\\\\nFALCON_CLIENT_ID=your-client-id\\\\nFALCON_CLIENT_SECRET=your-client-secret\\\\nFALCON_BASE_URL=https://api.crowdstrike.com\\\\n\\\\n# Optional Configuration (uncomment and modify as needed)\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_MODULES=detections,incidents,intel\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_TRANSPORT=stdio\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_DEBUG=false\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_HOST=127.0.0.1\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_PORT=8000\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_STATELESS_HTTP=false\\\\n#FALCON_MCP_API_KEY=your-api-key\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n#### Environment Variables\\\\n\\\\nAlternatively, you can use environment variables directly.\\\\n\\\\nSet the following environment variables in your shell:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Required Configuration\\\\nexport FALCON_CLIENT_ID=\\\\"your-client-id\\\\"\\\\nexport FALCON_CLIENT_SECRET=\\\\"your-client-secret\\\\"\\\\nexport FALCON_BASE_URL=\\\\"https://api.crowdstrike.com\\\\"\\\\n\\\\n# Optional Configuration\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_MODULES=\\\\"detections,incidents,intel\\\\"  # Comma-separated list (default: all modules)\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_TRANSPORT=\\\\"stdio\\\\"                     # Transport method: stdio, sse, streamable-http\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_DEBUG=\\\\"false\\\\"                         # Enable debug logging: true, false\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_HOST=\\\\"127.0.0.1\\\\"                      # Host for HTTP transports\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_PORT=\\\\"8000\\\\"                           # Port for HTTP transports\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_STATELESS_HTTP=\\\\"false\\\\"                # Stateless mode for scalable deployments\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_API_KEY=\\\\"your-api-key\\\\"                # API key for HTTP transport auth (x-api-key header)\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n**CrowdStrike API Region URLs:**\\\\n\\\\n* **US-1 (Default)**: `https://api.crowdstrike.com`\\\\n* **US-2**: `https://api.us-2.crowdstrike.com`\\\\n* **EU-1**: `https://api.eu-1.crowdstrike.com`\\\\n* **US-GOV**: `https://api.laggar.gcw.crowdstrike.com`\\\\n\\\\n### Installation\\\\n\\\\nNote\\\\n\\\\nIf you just want to interact with falcon-mcp via an agent chat interface rather than running the server itself, take a look at [Additional Deployment Options](#additional-deployment-options). Otherwise continue to the installations steps below.\\\\n\\\\n#### Install using uv\\\\n\\\\nuv tool install falcon-mcp\\\\n\\\\n#### Install using pip\\\\n\\\\npip install falcon-mcp\\\\n\\\\nTip\\\\n\\\\nIf `falcon-mcp` isn\\\'t found, update your shell PATH.\\\\n\\\\nFor installation via code editors/assistants, see the [Editor/Assitant](#editorassistant-integration) section below\\\\n\\\\n## Usage\\\\n\\\\n### Command Line\\\\n\\\\nRun the server with default settings (stdio transport):\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp\\\\n\\\\nRun with SSE transport:\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --transport sse\\\\n\\\\nRun with streamable-http transport:\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --transport streamable-http\\\\n\\\\nRun with streamable-http transport on custom port:\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --transport streamable-http --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8080\\\\n\\\\nRun with stateless HTTP mode (for scalable deployments like AWS AgentCore):\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --transport streamable-http --stateless-http\\\\n\\\\nRun with API key authentication (recommended for HTTP transports):\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --transport streamable-http --api-key your-secret-key\\\\n\\\\n> **Security Note**: When using HTTP transports (`sse` or `streamable-http`), consider enabling API key authentication via `--api-key` or `FALCON_MCP_API_KEY` to protect the endpoint. This is a self-generated key (any secure string you create) that ensures only authorized clients with the matching key can access the MCP server when running remotely. This is separate from your CrowdStrike API credentials.\\\\n\\\\n### Module Configuration\\\\n\\\\nThe Falcon MCP Server supports multiple ways to specify which modules to enable:\\\\n\\\\n#### 1. Command Line Arguments (highest priority)\\\\n\\\\nSpecify modules using comma-separated lists:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Enable specific modules\\\\nfalcon-mcp --modules detections,incidents,intel,spotlight,idp\\\\n\\\\n# Enable only one module\\\\nfalcon-mcp --modules detections\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n#### 2. Environment Variable (fallback)\\\\n\\\\nSet the `FALCON_MCP_MODULES` environment variable:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Export environment variable\\\\nexport FALCON_MCP_MODULES=detections,incidents,intel,spotlight,idp\\\\nfalcon-mcp\\\\n\\\\n# Or set inline\\\\nFALCON_MCP_MODULES=detections,incidents,intel,spotlight,idp falcon-mcp\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n#### 3. Default Behavior (all modules)\\\\n\\\\nIf no modules are specified via command line or environment variable, all available modules are enabled by default.\\\\n\\\\n**Module Priority Order:**\\\\n\\\\n1. Command line `--modules` argument (overrides all)\\\\n2. `FALCON_MCP_MODULES` environment variable (fallback)\\\\n3. All modules (default when none specified)\\\\n\\\\n### Additional Command Line Options\\\\n\\\\nFor all available options:\\\\n\\\\nfalcon-mcp --help\\\\n\\\\n### As a Library\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nfrom falcon_mcp.server import FalconMCPServer\\\\n\\\\n# Create and run the server\\\\nserver = FalconMCPServer(\\\\n    base_url=\\\\"https://api.us-2.crowdstrike.com\\\\",  # Optional, defaults to env var\\\\n    debug=True,  # Optional, enable debug logging\\\\n    enabled_modules=[\\\\"detections\\\\", \\\\"incidents\\\\", \\\\"spotlight\\\\", \\\\"idp\\\\"],  # Optional, defaults to all modules\\\\n    api_key=\\\\"your-api-key\\\\"  # Optional: API key for HTTP transport auth\\\\n)\\\\n\\\\n# Run with stdio transport (default)\\\\nserver.run()\\\\n\\\\n# Or run with SSE transport\\\\nserver.run(\\\\"sse\\\\")\\\\n\\\\n# Or run with streamable-http transport\\\\nserver.run(\\\\"streamable-http\\\\")\\\\n\\\\n# Or run with streamable-http transport on custom host/port\\\\nserver = FalconMCPServer(host=\\\\"0.0.0.0\\\\", port=8080)\\\\nserver.run(\\\\"streamable-http\\\\")\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n#### Direct Credentials (Secret Management Integration)\\\\n\\\\nFor enterprise deployments using secret management systems (HashiCorp Vault, AWS Secrets Manager, etc.), you can pass credentials directly instead of using environment variables:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nfrom falcon_mcp.server import FalconMCPServer\\\\n\\\\n# Example: Retrieve credentials from a secrets manager\\\\n# client_id = vault.read_secret(\\\\"crowdstrike/client_id\\\\")\\\\n# client_secret = vault.read_secret(\\\\"crowdstrike/client_secret\\\\")\\\\n\\\\n# Create server with direct credentials\\\\nserver = FalconMCPServer(\\\\n    client_id=\\\\"your-client-id\\\\",           # Or retrieved from vault/secrets manager\\\\n    client_secret=\\\\"your-client-secret\\\\",   # Or retrieved from vault/secrets manager\\\\n    base_url=\\\\"https://api.us-2.crowdstrike.com\\\\",  # Optional\\\\n    enabled_modules=[\\\\"detections\\\\", \\\\"incidents\\\\"]   # Optional\\\\n)\\\\n\\\\nserver.run()\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n> **Note**: When both direct parameters and environment variables are available, direct parameters take precedence.\\\\n\\\\n### Running Examples\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Run with stdio transport\\\\npython examples/basic_usage.py\\\\n\\\\n# Run with SSE transport\\\\npython examples/sse_usage.py\\\\n\\\\n# Run with streamable-http transport\\\\npython examples/streamable_http_usage.py\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n## Container Usage\\\\n\\\\nThe Falcon MCP Server is available as a pre-built container image for easy deployment:\\\\n\\\\n### Using Pre-built Image (Recommended)\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Pull the latest pre-built image\\\\ndocker pull quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest\\\\n\\\\n# Run with .env file (recommended)\\\\ndocker run -i --rm --env-file /path/to/.env quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest\\\\n\\\\n# Run with .env file and SSE transport\\\\ndocker run --rm -p 8000:8000 --env-file /path/to/.env \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest --transport sse --host 0.0.0.0\\\\n\\\\n# Run with .env file and streamable-http transport\\\\ndocker run --rm -p 8000:8000 --env-file /path/to/.env \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest --transport streamable-http --host 0.0.0.0\\\\n\\\\n# Run with .env file and custom port\\\\ndocker run --rm -p 8080:8080 --env-file /path/to/.env \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest --transport streamable-http --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8080\\\\n\\\\n# Run with .env file and specific modules (stdio transport - requires -i flag)\\\\ndocker run -i --rm --env-file /path/to/.env \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest --modules detections,incidents,spotlight,idp\\\\n\\\\n# Use a specific version instead of latest (stdio transport - requires -i flag)\\\\ndocker run -i --rm --env-file /path/to/.env \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:1.2.3\\\\n\\\\n# Alternative: Individual environment variables (stdio transport - requires -i flag)\\\\ndocker run -i --rm -e FALCON_CLIENT_ID=your_client_id -e FALCON_CLIENT_SECRET=your_secret \\\\\\\\\\\\n  quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n### Building Locally (Development)\\\\n\\\\nFor development or customization purposes, you can build the image locally:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Build the Docker image\\\\ndocker build -t falcon-mcp .\\\\n\\\\n# Run the locally built image\\\\ndocker run --rm -e FALCON_CLIENT_ID=your_client_id -e FALCON_CLIENT_SECRET=your_secret falcon-mcp\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nNote\\\\n\\\\nWhen using HTTP transports in Docker, always set `--host 0.0.0.0` to allow external connections to the container.\\\\n\\\\n## Editor/Assistant Integration\\\\n\\\\nYou can integrate the Falcon MCP server with your editor or AI assistant. Here are configuration examples for popular MCP clients:\\\\n\\\\n### Using `uvx` (recommended)\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n{\\\\n  \\\\"mcpServers\\\\": {\\\\n    \\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\": {\\\\n      \\\\"command\\\\": \\\\"uvx\\\\",\\\\n      \\\\"args\\\\": [\\\\n        \\\\"--env-file\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"/path/to/.env\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\"\\\\n      ]\\\\n    }\\\\n  }\\\\n}\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n### With Module Selection\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n{\\\\n  \\\\"mcpServers\\\\": {\\\\n    \\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\": {\\\\n      \\\\"command\\\\": \\\\"uvx\\\\",\\\\n      \\\\"args\\\\": [\\\\n        \\\\"--env-file\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"/path/to/.env\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"--modules\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"detections,incidents,intel\\\\"\\\\n      ]\\\\n    }\\\\n  }\\\\n}\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n### Using Individual Environment Variables\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n{\\\\n  \\\\"mcpServers\\\\": {\\\\n    \\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\": {\\\\n      \\\\"command\\\\": \\\\"uvx\\\\",\\\\n      \\\\"args\\\\": [\\\\"falcon-mcp\\\\"],\\\\n      \\\\"env\\\\": {\\\\n        \\\\"FALCON_CLIENT_ID\\\\": \\\\"your-client-id\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"FALCON_CLIENT_SECRET\\\\": \\\\"your-client-secret\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"FALCON_BASE_URL\\\\": \\\\"https://api.crowdstrike.com\\\\"\\\\n      }\\\\n    }\\\\n  }\\\\n}\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n### Docker Version\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n{\\\\n  \\\\"mcpServers\\\\": {\\\\n    \\\\"falcon-mcp-docker\\\\": {\\\\n      \\\\"command\\\\": \\\\"docker\\\\",\\\\n      \\\\"args\\\\": [\\\\n        \\\\"run\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"-i\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"--rm\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"--env-file\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"/full/path/to/.env\\\\",\\\\n        \\\\"quay.io/crowdstrike/falcon-mcp:latest\\\\"\\\\n      ]\\\\n    }\\\\n  }\\\\n}\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nNote\\\\n\\\\nThe `-i` flag is required when using the default stdio transport.\\\\n\\\\n## Additional Deployment Options\\\\n\\\\n### Amazon Bedrock AgentCore\\\\n\\\\nTo deploy the MCP Server as a tool in Amazon Bedrock AgentCore, please refer to the [following document](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/deployment/amazon_bedrock_agentcore.md).\\\\n\\\\n### Google Cloud (Cloud Run and Vertex AI)\\\\n\\\\nTo deploy the MCP server as an agent within Cloud Run or Vertex AI Agent Engine (including for registration within Agentspace), refer to the [Google ADK example](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/examples/adk/README.md).\\\\n\\\\n### Gemini CLI\\\\n\\\\n1. Install `uv`\\\\n2. `gemini extensions install https://github.com/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp`\\\\n3. Copy a valid `.env` file to `~/.gemini/extensions/falcon-mcp/.env`\\\\n\\\\n## Contributing\\\\n\\\\n### Getting Started for Contributors\\\\n\\\\n1. Clone the repository:\\\\n\\\\n   ```\\\\n   git clone https://github.com/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp.git\\\\n   cd falcon-mcp\\\\n   ```\\\\n2. Install in development mode:\\\\n\\\\n   ```\\\\n   # Create .venv and install dependencies\\\\n   uv sync --all-extras\\\\n\\\\n   # Activate the venv\\\\n   source .venv/bin/activate\\\\n   ```\\\\n\\\\nImportant\\\\n\\\\nThis project uses [Conventional Commits](https://www.conventionalcommits.org/) for automated releases and semantic versioning. Please follow the commit message format outlined in our [Contributing Guide](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/CONTRIBUTING.md) when submitting changes.\\\\n\\\\n### Running Tests\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n# Run all unit tests\\\\npytest\\\\n\\\\n# Run end-to-end tests (requires API credentials)\\\\npytest --run-e2e tests/e2e/\\\\n\\\\n# Run end-to-end tests with verbose output (note: -s is required to see output)\\\\npytest --run-e2e -v -s tests/e2e/\\\\n\\\\n# Run integration tests (requires API credentials)\\\\npytest --run-integration tests/integration/\\\\n\\\\n# Run integration tests with verbose output\\\\npytest --run-integration -v -s tests/integration/\\\\n\\\\n# Run integration tests for a specific module\\\\npytest --run-integration tests/integration/test_detections.py\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n> **Note**: The `-s` flag is required to see detailed output from E2E and integration tests.\\\\n\\\\n#### Integration Tests\\\\n\\\\nIntegration tests make real API calls to validate FalconPy operation names, HTTP methods, and response schemas. They catch issues that mocked unit tests cannot detect:\\\\n\\\\n* Incorrect FalconPy operation names (typos)\\\\n* HTTP method mismatches (POST body vs GET query parameters)\\\\n* Two-step search patterns not returning full details\\\\n* API response schema changes\\\\n\\\\n**Requirements**: Valid CrowdStrike API credentials must be configured (see [Environment Configuration](#environment-configuration)).\\\\n\\\\n### Developer Documentation\\\\n\\\\n* [Module Development Guide](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/development/module_development.md): Instructions for implementing new modules\\\\n* [Resource Development Guide](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/development/resource_development.md): Instructions for implementing resources\\\\n* [End-to-End Testing Guide](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/development/e2e_testing.md): Guide for running and understanding E2E tests\\\\n* [Integration Testing Guide](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/docs/development/integration_testing.md): Guide for running integration tests with real API calls\\\\n\\\\n## License\\\\n\\\\nThis project is licensed under the MIT License - see the [LICENSE](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/LICENSE) file for details.\\\\n\\\\n## Support\\\\n\\\\nThis is a community-driven, open source project. While it is not an official CrowdStroke product, it is actively maintained by CrowdStrike and supported in collaboration with the open source developer community.\\\\n\\\\nFor more information, please see our [SUPPORT](/CrowdStrike/falcon-mcp/blob/main/SUPPORT.md) file.\\\\n\\\\n## About\\\\n\\\\nConnect AI agents to CrowdStrike Falcon for automated security analysis and threat hunting\\\\n\\\\n### Topics\\\\n\\\\n[ai](/topics/ai \\\\"Topic: ai\\\\")\\\\n[mcp](/topics/mcp \\\\"Topic: mcp\\\\")\\\\n[falcon](/topics/falcon \\\\"Topic: falcon\\\\")\\\\n[crowdstrike](/topics/crowdstrike \\\\"Topic: crowdstrike\\\\")\\\\n[mcp-server](/topics/mcp-server \\\\"Topic: mcp-server\\\\")\\\\n\\\\n### Resources\\\\n\\\\n[Readme](#readme-ov-file)\\\\n\\\\n### License\\\\n\\\\n[MIT license](#MIT-1-ov-file)\\\\n\\\\n### Code of conduct\\\\n\\\\n[Code of conduct](#coc-ov-file)\\\\n\\\\n### Contributing\\\\n\\\\n[Contributing](#contributing-ov-file)\\\\n\\\\n### Security policy\\\\n\\\\n[Security policy](#security-ov-file)\\\\n\\\\n### Uh oh!\\\\n\\\\nThere was an error while loading. navigation\\\\n\\\\n# IPyIDA\\\\n\\\\nIPyIDA is a python-only solution to add an IPython console to IDA Pro. Use\\\\n`<Shift-.>` to open a window with an embedded *Qt console*. You can then\\\\nbenefit from IPython\\\\u2019s autocompletion, online help, monospaced font input\\\\nfield, graphs, and so on.\\\\n\\\\nYou can also connect to the kernel outside of IDA using `ipython console\\\\n--existing`.\\\\n\\\\n[![IPyIDA screenshot](https://github.com/eset/ipyida/raw/master/ipyida-screenshot.png)](/eset/ipyida/blob/master/ipyida-screenshot.png)\\\\n\\\\n## Install\\\\n\\\\nIPyIDA should be compatible with IDA 6.6 and later on Windows, OS X and Linux.\\\\nIt has been tested on IDA up to 9.2.\\\\n\\\\n### Fast and easy install\\\\n\\\\nA script is provided to install IPyIDA and its dependencies automagically from\\\\nthe IDA console. Simply copy the following line to the IDA console.\\\\n\\\\nPython 2\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nimport urllib2; exec urllib2.urlopen(\\\'https://github.com/eset/ipyida/raw/stable/install_from_ida.py\\\').read()\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nPython 3\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nimport urllib.request; exec(urllib.request.urlopen(\\\'https://github.com/eset/ipyida/raw/stable/install_from_ida.py\\\').read())\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nOn macOS, `Python3.framework` does not provide a trusted CA file. You can use\\\\nthe system-wide file `/etc/ssl/cert.pem`.\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nimport urllib.request; exec(urllib.request.urlopen(\\\'https://github.com/eset/ipyida/raw/stable/install_from_ida.py\\\', cafile=\\\\"/etc/ssl/cert.pem\\\\").read())\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nThe script will do the following:\\\\n\\\\n1. Install `pip` if it\\\\u2019s not already installed\\\\n2. Install the `ipyida` package from [PyPi](https://pypi.org/project/ipyida/)\\\\n3. Copy `ipyida_plugin_stub.py` to the user\\\\u2019s `plugins` directory\\\\n4. Load the IPyIDA plugin\\\\n\\\\nYou can inspect the [install\\\\\\\\_from\\\\\\\\_ida.py](/eset/ipyida/blob/master/install_from_ida.py) script if you wish to see\\\\nexactly what it does.\\\\n\\\\n#### Upgrading\\\\n\\\\nRerun the install script to update to the latest version and restart IDA.\\\\n\\\\n### Install it the IDA way\\\\n\\\\nIf you\\\\u2019d rather manage the dependencies and updates yourself, you can\\\\ncopy `ipyida_plugin_stub.py` and the `ipyida` directory inside IDA\\\\u2019s\\\\n`plugins` directory.\\\\n\\\\nThis method requires that you manage dependencies on your own. IPyIDA requires\\\\nthe `ipykernel` and `qtconsole` package, and the `qasync` package if using\\\\n`ipykernel` version 5 or newer.\\\\n\\\\n## Jupyter Notebook integration\\\\n\\\\nIPyIDA includes a magic command, `%open_notebook`, to open a browser with a\\\\nnotebook attached to IPyIDA. The command takes care of installing dependencies\\\\non its first run and starting a Notebook server unless one is already running.\\\\nCheck the command help (by typing `%open_notebook?`) for further options.\\\\n\\\\n## Customizing the IPython console\\\\n\\\\nBy default, the console does not have any globals available. If you want to\\\\nhave module imported before the console is opened, IPyIDA will read the\\\\n`ipyidarc.py` file from the IDA user directory (`idaapi.get_user_idadir()`).\\\\nAnything you import in this file will be available in the IPython console.\\\\n\\\\nThis is similar to the `idapythonrc.py` file.\\\\n\\\\n### Dark mode\\\\n\\\\nWith a dark theme in IDA Pro, it\\\\u2019s more convenient to also have a dark theme in\\\\nthe IPython console. To activate the dark theme built into `qtconsole`, add the\\\\nfollowing in your `ipyidarc.py`:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\nimport qtconsole.styles\\\\nimport ipyida.ida_qtconsole\\\\nipyida.ida_qtconsole.set_widget_options(dict(\\\\n    style_sheet = qtconsole.styles.default_dark_style_sheet,\\\\n    syntax_style = qtconsole.styles.default_dark_syntax_style\\\\n))\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n## IDE Integration\\\\n\\\\nOne of the noteworthy features of iPyIDA is the ability to integrate it with\\\\nthe PyCharm IDE. This allows features such as stepping through code,\\\\nsyntax highlighting, Github CoPilot integration, etc. To make use of this\\\\nfeature, simply launch IDA and open a database, create a Jupyter Notebook\\\\nin PyCharm, add some code, and click run. IPyIDA does all the magic in the\\\\nbackground.\\\\n\\\\n[![IPyIDA screenshot](https://github.com/eset/ipyida/raw/master/pycharm-screenshot.png)](/eset/ipyida/blob/master/pycharm-screenshot.png)\\\\n\\\\n## Caveats\\\\n\\\\n### External console not responding if IDA\\\\u2019s window is in the background for too long\\\\n\\\\nThis problem is specific to OS X\\\\u2019s App Nap feature in OS X 10.9 and up. When\\\\nrunning Disabling App Nap for IDA Pro seems to fix the problem, but is a a hack\\\\nfor now and will use more battery on a laptop, we should find a better solution.\\\\n\\\\nHere is how to disable App Nap for IDA Pro:\\\\n\\\\ndefaults write com.hexrays.idaq NSAppSleepDisabled -bool YES\\\\ndefaults write com.hexrays.idaq64 NSAppSleepDisabled -bool YES\\\\n\\\\n## Similar work\\\\n\\\\n@james91b also successfully integrated a IPython kernel in IDA. Being a\\\\nnon-Windows IDA user, I needed something cross-platform and took a Python-only\\\\napproach to implement it. Although the some of the implementation idea comes\\\\nfrom that project, IPyIDA was written from scratch. Hat tip to @james91b and all\\\\nIDA\\\\\\\\_IPython contributors. The analysis reveals significant patterns in tooling, methodologies, and architectural approaches that could enhance V-Sentinel\'s capabilities.\n\n**Analysis Date:** March 2026  \n**Organizations Analyzed:** Bitdefender, Malwarebytes, CrowdStrike, ESET  \n**Total Repositories Examined:** 15+ key repositories  \n\n---\n\n## 1. Key Findings Overview\n\n### 1.1 Most Relevant Findings for V-Sentinel\n\n| Finding | Organization | Relevance to V-Sentinel | Implementation Complexity |\n|---------|-------------|------------------------|--------------------------|\n| **AI Agent Integration via MCP** | CrowdStrike | ★★★★★ Critical | Medium |\n| **Instruction Disassembler & Emulator** | Bitdefender | ★★★★★ Critical | High |\n| **Hypervisor Memory Introspection** | Bitdefender | ★★★★ High | Very High |\n| **Malware IOC Repository Structure** | ESET | ★★★★ High | Low |\n| **Automated Security Deployment CLI** | Malwarebytes | ★★★ Medium | Low |\n| **VPN/Network Security Client** | Malwarebytes | ★★★ Medium | Medium |\n\n### 1.2 Technology Stack Patterns\n\n**Languages Most Commonly Used:**\n1. Python (dominant across all organizations)\n2. Go (gaining traction for security tools)\n3. C/C++ (for low-level security components)\n4. TypeScript (for modern web interfaces)\n5. YARA (for threat detection rules)\n\n**Architecture Patterns:**\n- Microservices-based APIs\n- Modular plugin architectures\n- Cloud-native deployments\n- Multi-language SDKs\n\n---\n\n## 2. Organization-Specific Analysis\n\n### 2.1 Bitdefender\n\n#### 2.1.1 Repository Overview\n\n**Total Repositories:** 28 public repositories  \n**Key Repositories Analyzed:**\n- `bddisasm` (1k+ stars) - Fast x86/x64 instruction decoder and emulator\n- `hvmi` (675+ stars, archived) - Hypervisor Memory Introspection Core Library\n- `napoca` (282+ stars, archived) - Lightweight type-1 hypervisor\n- `malware-ioc` (44 stars) - Indicators of Compromise for malware\n\n#### 2.1.2 Core Technologies Identified\n\n**1. bddisasm - Bitdefender Disassembler**\n- **Purpose:** Fast, lightweight x86/x64 instruction decoder with shellcode emulation capabilities\n- **Key Features:**\n  - No external dependencies\n  - Thread-safe by design\n  - Zero memory allocation\n  - Works in user, kernel, and hypervisor environments\n  - Comprehensive instruction metadata (operands, CPUID flags, access modes)\n  - Mini decoder API for performance optimization (64-byte INSTRUX_MINI vs 480-byte INSTRUX)\n- **Performance:** \n  - Legacy decoder: ~12M instructions/second\n  - Mini decoder: ~17M instructions/second\n- **Languages:** C (86%), Assembly (8.6%), Rust (2.9%), Python (2.2%)\n- **Build System:** CMake with vcpkg support\n- **Bindings:** Python and Rust\n\n**2. hvmi - Hypervisor Memory Introspection**\n- **Purpose:** Analyze guest VM state from outside using Intel VT-x\n- **Protection Capabilities:**\n  - Binary exploit prevention in protected processes\n  - Code/data injection blocking\n  - Function hook detection on system DLLs\n  - Rootkit prevention (inline hooks, SSDT hooks, Driver-object hooks)\n  - Kernel exploit protection\n  - Privilege escalation prevention\n  - Credentials theft blocking\n  - Deep process introspection\n  - Fileless malware detection (PowerShell command line scanning)\n- **Supported Hypervisors:** Napoca Hypervisor, Xen, KVM\n- **Architecture:** \n  - introcore (core library)\n  - CAMI (Guest support mechanism)\n  - Exceptions system (whitelisting legitimate accesses)\n- **Languages:** C (97.7%), Python (1.0%), C++ (0.8%)\n\n#### 2.1.3 V-Sentinel Improvement Opportunities\n\n**HIGH PRIORITY:**\n\n1. **Integrate Lightweight Disassembler**\n   - **Action:** Incorporate bddisasm or similar technology into V-Sentinel\'s malware analysis pipeline\n   - **Benefits:**\n     - Faster malware analysis (17M instructions/second)\n     - Shellcode detection capabilities\n     - No external dependencies (easier deployment)\n     - Works across all system levels (user, kernel, hypervisor)\n   - **Implementation:** \n     - Use as a library dependency via vcpkg\n     - Implement mini decoder API for performance-critical paths\n     - Create Python bindings for integration\n   - **Estimated Effort:** 2-3 months\n\n2. **Implement Memory Introspection Capabilities**\n   - **Action:** Develop hypervisor-level monitoring for advanced threat detection\n   - **Benefits:**\n     - Detect rootkits and kernel-level threats\n     - Prevent code injection attacks\n     - Monitor protected processes without affecting performance\n   - **Challenges:**\n     - Requires hypervisor support\n     - Complex integration (CAMI database, exception handling)\n   - **Estimated Effort:** 6-9 months (long-term strategic project)\n\n3. **Adopt CAMI-Style Guest Support System**\n   - **Action:** Create database-driven system for OS-specific threat detection patterns\n   - **Benefits:**\n     - Easier support for multiple OS versions\n     - Centralized pattern management\n     - Rapid response to new threats\n   - **Implementation:**\n     - Design pattern database schema\n     - Create pattern generation tools\n     - Implement runtime pattern matching\n   - **Estimated Effort:** 3-4 months\n\n**MEDIUM PRIORITY:**\n\n4. **Exception-Based Whitelisting System**\n   - **Action:** Implement flexible exception mechanism for legitimate system behaviors\n   - **Benefits:**\n     - Reduce false positives\n     - Allow legitimate security tools to operate\n     - Configurable per-environment rules\n   - **Implementation:** Similar to Bitdefender\'s exception binary format\n   - **Estimated Effort:** 2 months\n\n5. **Enhanced IOC Management**\n   - **Action:** Develop structured IOC repository similar to Bitdefender\'s malware-ioc\n   - **Benefits:**\n     - Better threat intelligence integration\n     - Community sharing capabilities\n     - Version-controlled detection rules\n   - **Estimated Effort:** 1-2 months\n\n#### 2.1.4 Best Practices from Bitdefender\n\n1. **Performance-First Design:**\n   - Zero-allocation architecture\n   - Thread-safe by default\n   - Multiple API levels (full vs mini decoder)\n   - Extensive benchmarking\n\n2. **Comprehensive Documentation:**\n   - Doxygen integration\n   - Sphinx-based specification documents\n   - Multiple build system support (CMake, Make, MSBuild)\n   - Example code and usage patterns\n\n3. **Multi-Platform Support:**\n   - Windows and Linux support out of the box\n   - Kernel and user-mode compatibility\n   - Multiple compiler support (GCC, Clang, MSVC)\n\n4. **Modular Architecture:**\n   - Clear separation of concerns (disassembler, emulator, tools)\n   - Plugin-based extensions\n   - Language bindings for different ecosystems\n\n---\n\n### 2.2 Malwarebytes\n\n#### 2.2.1 Repository Overview\n\n**Total Repositories:** 19 public repositories  \n**Key Repositories Analyzed:**\n- `ghas-cli` (5 stars) - Enhanced developer experience\n   - **Implementation:**\n     - Migrate from pip/poetry to uv\n     - Implement pyproject.toml configuration\n     - Set up pre-commit hooks with Ruff\n     - Automated testing with pytest\n   - Kubernetes operator\n- `omigo-data-analytics` (17+ stars) - Python data analytics library\n\n#### 2.3.2 Core Technologies Identified\n\n**1. falcon-mcp - Model Context Protocol Server (★★★★★ MOST INNOVATIVE)**\n- **Purpose:** Connect AI agents to CrowdStrike Falcon platform for automated security analysis\n- **Status:** Public Preview (actively developed)\n- **Architecture:**\n  - MCP server implementation with multiple transport options (stdio, SSE, streamable-http)\n  - Modular design with 13+ security modules\n  - Container deployment support (Docker)\n  - Multiple deployment options (Bedrock AgentCore, Google Cloud, Vertex AI)\n- **Modules Available:**\n  - **Cloud Security Module:** Kubernetes containers and image vulnerabilities\n  - **Detections Module:** Malicious activity analysis\n  - **Discover Module:** Application and unmanaged asset inventory\n  - **Hosts Module:** Host/device information management\n  - **Identity Protection Module:** Entity investigation with timeline analysis\n  - **Incidents Module:** Security incidents and behavior analysis\n  - **NGSIEM Module:** CQL query execution\n  - **Intel Module:** Threat actors, IOCs, and intelligence reports\n  - **IOC Module:** Custom IOC lifecycle management\n  - **Scheduled Reports Module:** Report automation\n  - **Sensor Usage Module:** Sensor deployment monitoring\n  - **Serverless Module:** Serverless function vulnerabilities\n  - **Spotlight Module:** Vulnerability management\n- **Key Features:**\n  - FQL (Falcon Query Language) guide resources for each module\n  - Per-module API scope configuration\n  - Educational content for each security feature\n  - Comprehensive testing (unit, integration, E2E)\n  - Developer documentation for module development\n- **Languages:** Python (98.7%), HTML (1.1%), Dockerfile (0.2%)\n- **Build System:** uv (Python package manager)\n- **Deployment Options:**\n  - Command-line tool (pip install)\n  - Docker containers (pre-built images available)\n  - Cloud platforms (AWS Bedrock, Google Cloud)\n  - Editor integration (Claude Desktop, Cursor, etc.)\n\n**2. gofalcon - Golang SDK**\n- **Purpose:** Comprehensive Golang SDK for CrowdStrike Falcon APIs\n- **Features:**\n  - Full API coverage\n  - Type-safe interfaces\n  - Concurrent request handling\n  - Comprehensive documentation\n- **Languages:** Go\n- **Usage:** Enterprise-grade integrations and high-performance applications\n\n**3. falconjs - JavaScript/TypeScript SDK**\n- **Purpose:** Browser and Node.js SDK for Falcon APIs\n- **Features:**\n  - Full API coverage\n  - TypeScript support for type safety\n  - Async/await patterns\n  - Browser and Node.js compatibility\n- **Languages:** TypeScript\n- **Usage:** Web applications and Node.js services\n\n**4. Infrastructure as Code Tools:**\n- **Terraform Provider:** Manage Falcon resources via Terraform\n- **Kubernetes Operator:** Deploy and manage Falcon in K8s environments\n- **Ansible Collection:** Automate Falcon operations via Ansible playbooks\n\n#### 2.3.3 V-Sentinel Improvement Opportunities\n\n**CRITICAL PRIORITY:**\n\n1. **Implement AI Agent Integration via MCP (★★★★★ HIGHEST IMPACT)**\n   - Indicators of Compromise repository\n- `ipyida` (836+ stars) - IPython console integration for IDA Pro\n- `malware-research` (409+ stars) - Malware investigation code\n- `vba-dynamic-hook` (153+ stars) - Cisco integration\n\n#### 2.4.2 Core Technologies Identified\n\n**1. malware-ioc - Indicators of Compromise Repository**\n- **Purpose:** Comprehensive IOC repository for malware investigations\n- **Scale:** 100+ malware families covered (A-Z index)\n- **Content Types:**\n  - YARA rules (.yar files)\n  - Snort rules (.rules files)\n  - Hash lists (MD5, SHA1, SHA256)\n  - Investigation documentation\n- **Notable Malware Families:**\n  - Advanced Persistent Threats (APTs): APT-C-60, Attor, BlackLotus, Dukes, etc.\n  - Ransomware: Emotet, Grandoreiro, Mekotio, etc.\n  - Botnets: Glupteba, Mozi, etc.\n  - Trojans: AsyncRAT, Danabot, Evilnum, etc.\n  - Espionage tools: CosmicBeetle, GoldenJackal, MoustachedBouncer, etc.\n- **Community Features:**\n  - BSD-2-Clause permissive license\n  - Pull request welcome for improvements\n  - Issue reporting for false positives\n  - Active community engagement\n- **Languages:** YARA (76.6%), Raku (16.8%), Python (4.1%)\n- **Impact:** 1.9k stars, 280 forks, 228 watchers\n\n**2. ipyida - Graph visualization capabilities\n  - External kernel connection\n  - Jupyter Notebook integration (%open_notebook magic command)\n  - PyCharm IDE integration for debugging\n  - Dark mode support\n  - Customizable via ipyidarc.py\n- **Compatibility:** IDA 6.6+ (tested up to IDA 9.2)\n- **Installation:** Automated installation script from IDA console\n- **Languages:** Python (100%)\n- **Impact:** 836 stars, 79 forks\n\n**3. malware-research - Malware Investigation Code**\n- **Purpose:** Research code from various malware investigations\n- **Content:** Python scripts and tools for malware analysis\n- **Languages:** Python\n- **Impact:** 409 stars, 89 forks\n\n**4. vba-dynamic-hook - Cross-Organization Analysis\n\n### 3.1 Common Patterns and Trends\n\n#### 3.1.1 Technology Stack Convergence\n\n**Languages:**\n- Python is universal (all organizations use it extensively)\n- Go is gaining traction for performance-critical components\n- TypeScript for modern web interfaces\n- C/C++ for low-level security components\n\n**Build Systems:**\n- Modern Python: uv (Malwarebytes, CrowdStrike)\n- Traditional: CMake (Bitdefender)\n- Containerization: Docker (all organizations)\n\n**Testing:**\n- pytest is standard for Python\n- Integration testing with real API calls (CrowdStrike)\n- E2E testing for complex workflows\n\n#### 3.1.2 Architecture Patterns\n\n1. **Microservices/Modular Design:**\n   - CrowdStrike\'s falcon-mcp with 13+ modules\n   - Bitdefender\'s separate components (disassembler, emulator, introspection)\n   - Per-feature configuration and deployment\n\n2. **Multi-Platform Support:**\n   - Windows and Linux support (all organizations)\n   - Kernel and user-mode compatibility\n   - Container-based deployments\n\n3. **API-First Design:**\n   - REST APIs (all organizations)\n   - GraphQL (CrowdStrike Identity Protection)\n   - gRPC (ESET\'s grpc-rest-proxy)\n\n4. **Cloud-Native Approach:**\n   - Kubernetes operators (CrowdStrike)\n   - Terraform providers (CrowdStrike)\n   - Cloud platform integrations (AWS, GCP, Azure)\n\n#### 3.1.3 Development Practices\n\n1. **Documentation Excellence:**\n   - Comprehensive README files\n   - Installation guides\n   - Usage examples\n   - API documentation\n   - Troubleshooting sections\n\n2. **Security-First Approach:**\n   - SECURITY.md files\n   - Vulnerability reporting processes\n   - Minimal dependencies\n   - Code scanning (CodeQL)\n\n3. **Community Engagement:**\n   - Open-source repositories\n   - Permissive licensing (MIT, BSD, Apache-2.0)\n   - Contribution guidelines\n   - Issue tracking and management\n\n4. **Automation and CI/CD:**\n   - GitHub Actions workflows\n   - Automated testing\n   - Release automation\n   - Pre-commit hooks\n\n### 3.2 Competitive Advantages Analysis\n\n#### 3.2.1 Bitdefender\'s Advantages\n\n**Strengths:**\n1. Deep technical expertise in low-level security (hypervisor, disassembler)\n2. Performance-optimized code (zero-allocation, thread-safe)\n3. Comprehensive documentation (Doxygen, Sphinx)\n4. Multi-platform support (Windows, Linux, kernel, user-mode)\n\n**For V-Sentinel:**\n- Learn from performance optimization techniques\n- Adopt multi-platform support early\n- Invest in comprehensive documentation\n\n#### 3.2.2 Malwarebytes\' Advantages\n\n**Strengths:**\n1. Modern development practices (uv, pyproject.toml)\n2. Excellent CLI design (educational content, extensive options)\n3. Security-focused development (capabilities, minimal deps)\n4. Network security expertise (VPN implementation)\n\n**For V-Sentinel:**\n- Adopt modern Python tooling\n- Focus on developer experience\n- Implement network security monitoring\n\n#### 3.2.3 CrowdStrike\'s Advantages\n\n**Strengths:**\n1. AI-first architecture (MCP server)\n2. Multi-language SDK ecosystem\n3. Infrastructure as Code support\n4. Modular design with per-feature configuration\n5. Extensive integration ecosystem\n\n**For V-Sentinel:**\n- Implement AI agent integration ASAP\n- Develop multi-language SDKs\n- Create IaC tooling\n- Adopt modular architecture\n\n#### 3.2.4 ESET\'s Advantages\n\n**Strengths:**\n1. Strong community engagement (malware-ioc with 1.9k stars)\n2. Analyst-focused tools (ipyida, DelphiHelper)\n3. Research transparency and knowledge sharing\n4. Specialized expertise in niche areas\n\n**For V-Sentinel:**\n- Build public IOC repository\n- Develop analyst productivity tools\n- Share research publicly\n- Focus on niche expertise\n\n### 3.3 Gaps and Opportunities for V-Sentinel\n\n#### 3.3.1 Identified Gaps\n\n1. **No AI Agent Integration:**\n   - CrowdStrike has falcon-mcp\n   - V-Sentinel needs similar capability\n   - **Priority:** CRITICAL\n\n2. **Limited Public Presence:**\n   - ESET has 1.9k-star IOC repository\n   - V-Sentinel needs community-facing repositories\n   - **Priority:** HIGH\n\n3. **No Multi-Language SDKs:**\n   - CrowdStrike has Python, Go, TypeScript SDKs\n   - V-Sentinel needs SDK ecosystem\n   - **Priority:** HIGH\n\n4. **Missing IaC Support:**\n   - CrowdStrike has Terraform provider, K8s operator\n   - V-Sentinel needs cloud-native deployment tools\n   - **Priority:** MEDIUM\n\n5. **No Automated Deployment Tools:**\n   - Malwarebytes has ghas-cli\n   - V-Sentinel needs deployment automation\n   - **Priority:** MEDIUM\n\n6. **Limited Analyst Tools:**\n   - ESET has ipyida, DelphiHelper\n   - V-Sentinel needs reverse engineering tools\n   - **Priority:** MEDIUM\n\n#### 3.3.2 Market Opportunities\n\n1. **AI-Driven Security Operations:**\n   - First-mover advantage with MCP implementation\n   - Natural language interfaces for security\n   - Automated threat hunting and analysis\n\n2. **Community Threat Intelligence:**\n   - Build large-scale IOC repository\n   - Become thought leader in threat intel\n   - Encourage community contributions\n\n3. **Developer-Friendly Security Platform:**\n   - Comprehensive SDKs for multiple languages\n   - Easy integration and adoption\n   - Extensive documentation and examples\n\n4. **Cloud-Native Security:**\n   - Kubernetes-native deployments\n   - Infrastructure as Code support\n   - Multi-cloud compatibility\n\n---\n\n## 4. sentinel_threat_intel import IOCGenerator\n\ndef generate_from_incidents(incident_data):\n    """Generuj IOC z danych incydentów V-Sentinel"""\n    generator = IOCGenerator()\n    \n    # YARA rules\n    yara_rules = generator.create_yara_rules(incident_data)\n    \n    # Hash lists\n    md5_hashes = generator.extract_md5(incident_data)\n    sha256_hashes = generator.extract_sha256(incident_data)\n    \n    return {\n        \'yara\': yara_rules,\n        \'md5\': md5_hashes,\n        \'sha256\': sha256_hashes\n    }\n```\n\n**Tydzień 5-6: Dokumentacja i Automatyzacja**\n- README z przykładami ["setuptools>=61.0"]\nbuild-backend = "setuptools.build_meta"\n\n[project]\nname = "sentinel-sdk"\nversion = "0.1.0"\ndescription = "Official V-Sentinel Python SDK"\nrequires-python = ">=3.11"\ndependencies = [\n    "httpx>=0.25.0",\n    "pydantic>=2.0.0",\n    "aiohttp>=3.9.0",\n]\n```\n\n**Struktura SDK:**\n```\nsentinel_sdk/\n├── __init__.py\n├── client.py           # Główny klient API\n├── auth.py             # Autentykacja\n├── modules/\n│   ├── __init__.py\n│   ├── detections.py   # Moduł detekcji\n│   ├── hosts.py        # Moduł hostów\n│   ├── incidents.py    # Moduł incydentów\n│   └── threat_intel.py # Wywiad zagrożeń\n└── utils/\n    ├── __init__.py\n    └── helpers.py\n```\n\n**Implementacja Core Client:**\n```python\n# sentinel_sdk/client.py\nimport httpx\nfrom typing import Optional\nfrom sentinel_sdk.auth import AuthProvider\n\nclass SentinelClient:\n    """Klient API V-Sentinel"""\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        api_key: str,\n        base_url: str = "https://api.sentinel.io",\n        timeout: int = 30\n    ):\n        self.api_key = api_key\n        self.base_url = base_url\n        self.timeout = timeout\n        \n        # HTTP client\n        self.client = httpx.AsyncClient(\n            base_url=base_url,\n            headers={"Authorization": f"Bearer {api_key}"},\n            timeout=timeout\n        )\n        \n        # Moduły\n        from sentinel_sdk.modules import (\n            DetectionsModule,\n            HostsModule,\n            IncidentsModule,\n            ThreatIntelModule\n        )\n        \n        self.detections = DetectionsModule(self)\n        self.hosts = HostsModule(self)\n        self.incidents = IncidentsModule(self)\n        self.threat_intel = ThreatIntelModule(self)\n    \n    async def close(self):\n        """Zamknij połączenie"""\n        await self.client.aclose()\n```\n\n**Miesiąc 4: Moduły Advanced**\n```python\n# sentinel_sdk/modules/detections.py\nfrom typing import List, Dict, Optional\nfrom sentinel_sdk.utils import parse_response\n\nclass DetectionsModule:\n    """Moduł do zarządzania detekcjami"""\n    \n    def __init__(self, client: SentinelClient):\n        self.client = client\n    \n    async def search(\n        self,\n        query: str,\n        limit: int = 100,\n        offset: int = 0\n    ) -> List[Dict]:\n        """Wyszukaj detekcje"""\n        response = await self.client.client.post(\n            "/api/v1/detections/search",\n            json={\n                "query": query,\n                "limit": limit,\n                "offset": offset\n            }\n        )\n        return parse_response(response)\n    \n    async def get_details(self, detection_id: str) -> Dict:\n        """Pobierz szczegóły detekcji"""\n        response = await self.client.client.get(\n            f"/api/v1/detections/{detection_id}"\n        )\n        return parse_response(response)\n```\n\n**Miesiąc 5: Dokumentacja i Testing**\n```python\n# examples/basic_usage.py\nimport asyncio\nfrom sentinel_sdk import SentinelClient\n\nasync def main():\n    # Inicjalizacja klienta\n    client = SentinelClient(\n        api_key="your-api-key"\n    )\n    \n    try:\n        # Wyszukaj detekcje\n        detections = await client.detections.search(\n            query="severity:critical",\n            limit=10\n        )\n        \n        print(f"Znaleziono {len(detections)} krytycznych detekcji")\n        \n        # Pobierz szczegóły\n        for detection in detections:\n            details = await client.detections.get_details(\n                detection["id"]\n            )\n            print(f"Detekcja: {details[\'name\']}")\n    \n    finally:\n        await client.close()\n\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    asyncio.run(main())\n```\n\n**Miesiąc 6: PyPI Release**\n```bash\n# Budowanie i publikacja\npython -m build\ntwine upload dist/*\n```\n\n#### Priorytet 3.2: Go SDK (Miesiące 5-7)\n\n**Struktura Go SDK:**\n```\nsrc/go-sdk/\n├── go.mod\n├── go.sum\n├── README.md\n├── client.go           # Główny klient\n├── auth.go             # "context"\n    "net/http"\n)\n\ntype Client struct {\n    apiKey    string\n    baseURL   string\n    httpClient *http.Client\n    \n    // Moduły\n    Detections *DetectionsModule\n    Hosts      *HostsModule\n    Incidents  *IncidentsModule\n    ThreatIntel *ThreatIntelModule\n}\n\nfunc NewClient(apiKey string, opts ...ClientOption) *Client {\n    client := &Client{\n        apiKey: apiKey,\n        baseURL: "https://api.sentinel.io",\n        httpClient: &http.Client{},\n    }\n    \n    // Konfiguracja opcji\n    for _, opt := range opts {\n        opt(client)\n    }\n    \n    // Inicjalizacja modułów\n    client.Detections = &DetectionsModule{client: client}\n    client.Hosts = &HostsModule{client: client}\n    client.Incidents = &IncidentsModule{client: client}\n    client.ThreatIntel = &ThreatIntelModule{client: client}\n    \n    return client\n}\n```\n\n#### Priorytet 3.3: TypeScript SDK (Miesiące 6-8)\n\n**Struktura TypeScript SDK:**\n```\nsrc/ts-sdk/\n├──
